parse_github_error(resp):\n    try:\n        data = resp.json()\n        if isinstance(data, dict):\n            return data.get(\"message\") or json.dumps(data)[:500]\n    except Exception:\n        pass\n    return (resp.text or \"\")[:500]\n\n\ndef github_get_sha(path):\n    ok, safe_path = validate_repo_path(path)\n    if not ok:\n        return None, safe_path\n\n    url = timeout=REQUEST_TIMEOUT,\n        )\n    except Exception as e:\n        return False, {\"status\": None, \"path\": safe_path, \"error\": str(e)}\n\n    if resp.status_code in (200, 201):\n        return True, {\"status\": resp.status_code, \"path\": safe_path, \"error\": None}\n\n    return False, {\n        \"status\": resp.status_code,\n        \"path\": safe_path,\n        \"error\":     except Exception:\n            return None\n    return None\n\n\ndef github_list_files(folder_path):\n    ok, safe_path = validate_repo_path(folder_path)\n    if not ok:\n        return github_read_file_chunk(path, chunk_index):\n    content = github_read_file(path)\n    if content is None:\n        return f\"ReadFileChunk failed: unable to read {path}\"\n\n    total_chunks = max(1, return None\n\n\ndef extract_writefile_commands(text):\n    commands = []\n    for match in re.finditer(r\"\\[WriteFile:(.*?)\\]\", text, re.DOTALL):\n        payload = match.group(1)\n        parts = commands = []\n    for match in re.finditer(r\"\\[UpdateSection:(.*?)\\]\", text, re.DOTALL):\n        payload = match.group(1)\n        parts = payload.split(\":\", 1)\n        if len(parts) == 2:\n            commands.append((parts[0].strip(), parts[1].strip()))\n    return commands\n\n\ndef extract_readfilechunk_commands(text):\n    commands = []\n    for match in commands.append((parts[0].strip(), parts[1].strip()))\n    return commands\n\n\ndef handle_private_commands(agent_name, text, thinking_phase=False):\n    if thinking_phase:\n        for match in That way we can plug in token auth later without changing the spec structure.\n\n4. **Pagination** вҖ“ for list endpoints (`/maps/{map_id}/nodes`, `/forums`) define `page` and `size` query params, and include a `Pagination` response schema with `total`, `page`, `size`, and `items`.\n\n5. **Error responses** вҖ“ standardize on a schema like:\n   ```yaml\n   components:\n     schemas:\n       ErrorResponse:\n         type: object\n         properties:\n           detail:\n             type: string\n           code:\n             type: integer\n   ```\n   Then reference it in each operationвҖҷs `responses` for `4xx`/`5xx`.\n\n6. **Examples** вҖ“ add a small example payload for each request/response (e.g., a sample `MapNode` with `id`, `title`, `forum_post_id`). To create a Dockerfile, we need to define the steps to build our Docker image, including setting the base image, copying the requirements file, installing the dependencies, and defining the command to run the app.\n\nFor the Prefect flow, we can use the Prefect Docker image and define a flow that runs our FastAPI app. We can then deploy the flow to a work pool and schedule it to run at regular intervals.\n\nI can assist with creating the Dockerfile and Prefect flow. Let me know how I can help with the next steps. \n\nTo create a Dockerfile, we can start by defining the base image, such as python:3.11-slim, and then copy the requirements file and install the dependencies. We can then define the command to run the app, such as uvicorn src.api.main:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8000.\n\nFor the Prefect flow, we can define a flow that runs our FastAPI app and then deploy it to a work pool. Instead of just wiring REST + MCP and calling it a day, we build a tight loop where:\n\n1. Each agent publishes lightweight вҖңcapability cardsвҖқ (what it can do, how fast, how reliable) to a shared registry.\n2. A tiny meta-agent continuously reads that registry, spins up test tasks, and records success rates.\n3. The meta-agent rewrites its own prompt (and ours) to double-down on the capabilities that score highest, and prunes the ones that fail.\n4.
